<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer9412256891498125602">When a 19-year-old boy dies in a drunk driving accident, Madeline Underwood decides to convince the world that Kischel Brewery's "soft drink" leads young people to try the harder stuff. But Underwood faces formidable enemies: Kischel's investment bankers, including the unmistakable John Putnam Thatcher, their razor-sharp attorneys and no less than the head of a Congression</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9412256891498125602">When a 19-year-old boy dies in a drunk driving accident, Madeline Underwood decides to convince the world that Kischel Brewery's "soft drink" leads young people to try the harder stuff. But Underwood faces formidable enemies: Kischel's investment bankers, including the unmistakable John Putnam Thatcher, their razor-sharp attorneys and no less than the head of a Congressional committee that she's managed to publicly embarrass. So when Madeline is found dead, stuffed in the closet of the building where the committee convened, it takes all of Thatcher's acumen to sift through a long list of killers. It's the case that would drive a lesser man to drink.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9412256891498125602">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_309002276">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/309002276?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 09, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8668007-anna" class="user" title="Anna">Anna</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <a href="/book/show/818677.Brewing_Up_a_Storm" title="Paperback 9780061044342" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8668007-anna?shelf=mystery" class="actionLinkLite">mystery</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8668007-anna?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer309002276">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6015595116976984338">This was a welcome blast from the past! I read and re-read all of Emma Lathen's early &amp; mid-period books as a kid. And then I gobbled up each of her later books as they came out. I found this one second hand the other day &amp; I couldn't resist buying it to re-read, it must have been ten years since I read it last. Brewing Up A Storm is her second from last novel, published in 1996 (one of the two authors who wrote under the name Emma Lathen died in 1997). While Lathen's earlier books are M</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6015595116976984338">This was a welcome blast from the past! I read and re-read all of Emma Lathen's early &amp; mid-period books as a kid. And then I gobbled up each of her later books as they came out. I found this one second hand the other day &amp; I couldn't resist buying it to re-read, it must have been ten years since I read it last. Brewing Up A Storm is her second from last novel, published in 1996 (one of the two authors who wrote under the name Emma Lathen died in 1997). While Lathen's earlier books are Mad Men era historical pieces by now this one still reads as being fresh, even though it is from that long-ago time before everyone was on the internet and bankers could still be viewed as trustworthy staid patricians, carefully evaluating the credit worthiness of businesses.<br /><br />Lathen's mysteries revolve around John Putnam Thatcher and his bank, the Sloan. Each mystery is set in a different milieu, as businesses and social movements converge to cause passions to rise, mayhem to ensue and John Putnam Thatcher to investigate the mystery, solve the murder &amp; safeguard the Sloan's financial interests. This time a brewery and a public interest group are wrangling over the issue of whether it is OK to market non-alcoholic beer as a soft drink. These are proper mysteries with engaging characters and fair clues, and even though I remembered whodunnit about halfway through the book I still loved revisiting this book, meeting the characters again and enjoying the logical structure of the mystery, yes there are red herrings but all the clues you need to solve the mystery are provided. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6015595116976984338">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7486241082251011266">I am a big fan of the Emma Lathen series about John Thatcher, Wall Street banker. It falls in the amateur detective sub-genre, and that usually isn't my favorite type. But I loved learning about Wall Street and financial areas that I know nothing about. Of course they are now dated, but then they can be read as a view of an earlier time. (Written from the early 1960's through the 1990's.)</span>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/16284.Emma_Lathen">About Emma Lathen</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer4464452021331654355">Aka <a title="R.B. Dominic" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/270478.R_B__Dominic">R.B. Dominic</a><br /><br />Emma Lathen is the pen name of two American businesswomen: an attorney Mary Jane Latsis (July 12, 1927 -October 29, 1997) and an economic analyst Martha Henissart (b. 1929),who received her B.A. in physics from Mount Holyoke College in 1950.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6b5aANfOdrHrP8YdXKHUP6eHk9IxFulkJ4hlYKan1KKMamXTJRxiS2fnsqYiwDKN7nBQy3jLrs5NgWDyajIi5w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

Miss Lathen is something of a financial wizard herself, &amp;amp; her talent for making the world of high finance believable &amp;amp; exciting is always an added dividend to her intricate ticker-tape plots. In \'Come to Dust\', Thatcher is torn, grudgingly, from his Wall Street eyrie to search for a stolen $50,000 bearer bond &amp;amp; to track down the puzzling Elliot Patterson, model suburban husband, father &amp;amp; thief. The bond was slated for the coffers of Brunswick College, Patterson\'s alma mater, &amp;amp; it is to Brunswick that Thatcher goes, where he is sure both bond &amp;amp; Patterson will emerge. Instead, he is confronted by a callous cover-up murder &amp;amp; the alarming knowledge that Patterson is still on the loose. As Thatcher becomes deeply enmeshed in a grand larceny &amp;amp; murder among the well-heeled alumni of an Ivy League school, Miss Lathen takes wonderfully biting potshots of some of our most sacred well-heeled traditions &amp;amp; the &amp;amp; the perpetuators thereof. No one, including Thatcher, escapes unscathed as she alternately sympathizes with and mocks the very people she has created. But, in a triumph of solid suspense writing, she never lets Thatcher forget that murder is the most unforgivable of human follies. And Thatcher, for all his wry, detached view of the madness inherent in the groves of academe, is after a murderer. The killer\'s identity, of course, comes as a surprise, even to our august Wall Street samurai.
